    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2068284830" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2068284830" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/945939-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529617149p2/945939.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2068284830?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/945939-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/945939-kathryn?shelf=ya-realistic-fic">ya-realistic-fic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/945939-kathryn?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2068284830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4687211552447811039"><b>A book steeped in fandom and set in Charleston, SC?</b> Yes, please! Seriously, Ashley Poston’s <i>Geekerella</i> has ME written all over it. You’ve got my parents’ hometown (Charleston) combined with a fairy tale retelling (one of my fave subgenres) infused with a fandom-centric plot. <b>Be still my nerdy soul! </b><br/><br/>As fandom becomes increasingly mainstream more books are being published featuring this unique culture. And what’s better, they’re representing it WELL. <i>Fangirl</i> by Rainbow Rowell and <i>Eliza and her Mon</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4687211552447811039" style="display:none"><b>A book steeped in fandom and set in Charleston, SC?</b> Yes, please! Seriously, Ashley Poston’s <i>Geekerella</i> has ME written all over it. You’ve got my parents’ hometown (Charleston) combined with a fairy tale retelling (one of my fave subgenres) infused with a fandom-centric plot. <b>Be still my nerdy soul! </b><br /><br />As fandom becomes increasingly mainstream more books are being published featuring this unique culture. And what’s better, they’re representing it WELL. <i>Fangirl</i> by Rainbow Rowell and <i>Eliza and her Monsters</i> by Francesca Zappia are two recent examples. <b>No longer is fandom considered the domain of the weird and socially inept.</b> Fandom-centric books are bringing forth this formerly insular world and revealing the genius and creativity present within. <br /><br />Since I’m a wee bit older than the standard fangirl, (most of) my IRL friends and/or family never experienced this phenomenon. It was never a <i>thing</i> when they were growing up. So to them fan culture seems obsessive, pointless, and downright <b>WEIRD.</b> How can you possibly be friends with people you’ve never met? But here’s what they don’t understand: fandom friendships can be as genuine and authentic as any real life relationship. The bond created by shared, fevered interests is both intense and immediate. <b>Basically I’m speaking Klingon and the only people who can translate my wacky are my cyber-space compatriots. </b><br /><br /><i>Geekerella</i><b> not only gets fandom, it celebrates it.</b> Based on the traditional Cinderella story, <i>Geekerella</i> has <b>all the trappings of the oft-repeated fairy tale but twisted to fit a contemporary setting. </b> Yes, we have the requisite beleaguered title character tormented by her evil stepmother &amp; stepsisters. But every other classic feature has been realistically adjusted. <b>The prince is actually a movie star, the carriage is a pumpkin-themed food truck, and the famous glass slipper? Cosplay. </b><i>Geekerella’s</i> <b>strength lies in its creativity.</b> Making what could have been nonsensical, both relevant and applicable. <br /><br />And that relevance extends to our main character’s name, Elle. <b>An orphaned, friendless Elle lives in Charleston’s historic section alongside her stepmother and stepsisters.</b> Tormented daily, Elle is desperate to escape and perceives an upcoming con (for all you fandom virgins, think: comic con) as her ticket out. <b>Elle is a diehard Starfield fan</b>, a classic sci-fi show similarly loved by her late parents. ExcelsiCon features a planned cosplay contest. What’s even better than dressing up as your fave Starfield character? Getting paid to do so. <b>If Elle wins the contest, the prize money will fund a move to Los Angeles. Adios, jerks. </b><br /><br />This year’s ExcelsiCon is doubly exciting because <b>Darien Freeman, star of the long-awaited Starfield movie, will be present.</b> Soap stud Darien brings with him hoardes of screaming fans drooling over his rockhard abs. <b>But you know who’s not drooling? Elle. She has zero interest in Twilight-ing her favorite show.</b> She wants appreciation and depth. Not Robert Pattinson-esque frenzy. Twihards be damned. To her Darien is a dime a dozen soap hunk with no knowledge or respect for Starfield. <b>A blog post detailing why Darien is a poor casting choice propels Elle’s little side project to stratospheric proportions.</b> And in the midst of the hub-bub? A dismayed Darien. After reading Elle’s harsh criticism Darien, secretly a genuine Starfield fan, contacts ExcelsiCon organizers to cancel his appearance. <b>But you can’t escape fate (or fairy tale magic) </b>because d’ya know who founded ExcelsiCon? Elle’s late father. <b>After Darien’s message is mistakenly forwarded to Elle’s phone, an anonymous relationship via text is formed.</b> Basically, it’s like Cinderella meets Who’s Got Mail. From there the standard Cinderella story ensues. Chapters alternate between Elle and Darien, providing our “Prince Charming” the depth missing from the original fairy tale. <br /><br /><i>Geekerella</i> does a great job of taking the much beloved Cinderella tale and giving it modern flair. We’ve got<b> LGBTQA representation, a heroine with agency paired with a prince that’s a person of color, vlogging,</b> and more. The <b>early text-based relationship between Elle and Darien prevents the story from falling into fairy tale insta-love territory.</b> A solid foundation is formed before these two lovebirds even lock eyes making the story both refreshing and realistic. <br /><br />But while <i>Geekerella</i> is <b>realistic and undoubtedly adorable,</b> there’s <b>nothing groundbreaking to be found.</b> Yes it’s a modern twist, but <b>all the familiar Cinderella plot points remain.</b> It’s predictable. But that’s <b>not necessarily a bad thing.</b> Romantic comedies flourish in part due to their guaranteed happily-ever-after. In a world that’s so unbelievably random, it’s comforting to have something to rely on. <i>Geekerella</i> provides that.<br /><br /><b>To sum up:</b> Geekerella is a modern, romantic-comedy spin on Cinderella. <b>Definitely cute, but not necessarily a stand-out.</b> Early parts dragged a bit and while I appreciated the opportunity to delve into the “Prince’s” story, I found his sections slightly tedious. Thankfully, the story speeds up in the last quarter and at that point you’ll be glued to your seat. <br /><br /><b>Definitely a book I’d recommend to interested parties, but not a priority read.</b><br /><br /><b>3.5 stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4687211552447811039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11318751075622382141" style="display:none">This was cute as shit, omg.               <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=not-fantasy-2020">not-fantasy-2020</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3289090143" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14307253034646875480">Awwwww, I really enjoyed that!!! It was just so sweet, yet also powerful of a book and to be fair, I needed a book with a happy ending. It wasn’t perfect, hence the four stars, but still, it was just something joyous to read in a difficult time for everyone. I’m oddly in the mood for some cute, lighthearted, contemporaries books(preferably YA) so please hit me up with recs! 😄</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VeThG5E/PywsEv20pOONdUvt6ww3yAZPo5fhXrZW/dO6V4rGGqxObT1PIb11NidtDoewQvtrWwv32m5VhW/EnA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Wa17KLK2XZjjdyk2D8Op+UVqUmH1Voitmz5zcw57LWO2HhD1OSUs2fIq9T/eFgPhAAAJLzn11enPc/x4PUIULA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
